## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear classical mechanics / nonlinear oscillations
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x and time t. The acceleration encodes the restoring force (nonlinear in x), possible damping, and possible external driving forces (periodic in t).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (driven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (cubic nonlinearity with periodic driving)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (polynomial restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (linear spring with harmonic drive)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Driven nonlinear with quadratic and cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (general polynomial + drive)
- Nonlinear with position-dependent forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * sin(c3 * t) (mixed coupling)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric excitation)
- Rational restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x / (1 + c1 * x**2) (bounded nonlinear restoring force)
- Combined polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential energy
- Even-power terms (x²) in restoring force break symmetry → asymmetric oscillation with drift
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms additive to restoring force → forced oscillation
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling x*cos(c*t) → time-modulated stiffness leading to parametric resonance
- Negative linear coefficient (c0 < 0 for c0*x) with positive cubic (c1 > 0 for c1*x³) indicates double-well Duffing potential
- Sinusoidal dependence on position sin(c*x) indicates periodic potential or pendulum-like geometry
- Absence of explicit velocity variable suggests conservative system or that damping/velocity effects are encoded through the x(t) trajectory
- Rational functions of x like x/(1+c*x²) model saturation of restoring force at large displacements
